Existence as a Mere Label
Additional response: existence as a mere label

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the term 'existence' can be interpreted as a mere label that encompasses all particular existences, and why this avoids the need to posit a common real essence.

Core Idea
Existence as a label: one word covering all without requiring a shared reality.

In this passage, the author addresses an objection about the common meaning of existence. He first uses an analogy about 'no common person between two' to illustrate that denying a common subject does not require that subject to exist. Then he offers a second, more direct answer: the term 'existence' is used as a label (ism) that applies to all particular existences. This single meaning covers all particularities, allowing general judgments without proving each particular individually.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the two distinct parts: the analogy and the labeling response.
The analogy may seem abstract at first, but it sets up the logical principle.
2
Understand the analogy
The analogy: saying 'there is no common person between two' does not imply a common person exists; it only requires conceiving such a person. This shows that a negative statement about existence does not entail real existence of the subject.
This principle about negative propositions is key in logic.
3
Grasp the labeling theory
The second answer: 'existence' is just a word that names a single meaning covering all particular things. Judgments can be made about all existences through this label without needing to prove each particularity.
This avoids the need to assume a real common essence of existence.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument defends the position that existence is not a real predicate but a mere label. How does this affect theological discussions about God's existence?
This connects to broader debates in Islamic theology about the nature of existence.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما يقال : لا يوجد شخص مشترك فيه بين اثنين فإنه لا يقتضي شخصاً مشتركاً بينهما لاستحالته بل يقتضي تصوره ) وتحقيقه أن السالبة لا تقتضي وجود الموضوع)، بل تصوره فقط، ويمكن أن يجاب أيضاً بأن المراد بالوجود هو المسمى بلفظ الوجود، وهذا معنى واحد شامل لجميع الخصوصيات، فيحكم عليه حكماً لها بهذا العنوان المتناول إياها من غير حاجة إلى أن يبرهن على خصوصية كل واحد منها
Just as it is said: There is no common person between two, for that does not entail a common person between them due to its impossibility, but rather it entails conceiving him. And its verification is that the negative does not entail the existence of the subject, but rather only its conception. And it can also be answered that what is meant by existence is that which is named by the word 'existence', and this is a single meaning inclusive of all particularities, so judgment is made upon it for them by this title that encompasses them, without needing to prove the particularity of each one of them.

Commentary
This passage provides an additional response to the earlier objection. It first draws an analogy: saying 'there is no common person between two' does not imply a common person exists; it only requires conceiving such a person. Similarly, the negative proposition about existence does not imply a real common existence. Then a second answer is given: the term 'existence' is taken as a label (the name 'existence') that applies to all particular existences. This label is a single meaning that encompasses all particulars, and judgments can be made about them through this label without needing to prove each particularity individually. Thus, the opponent does not need to assume a real common essence of existence.

The Sixth Argument: Existence as a Single Meaning
The sixth argument and its initial response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth argument that if existence were not a single common meaning, the Necessary and contingent could not be distinguished, and how the response refutes it.

Core Idea
Distinguishing Necessary from contingent requires a single meaning of existence.

The sixth argument (al-wajh al-sadis) is a key objection against the view that existence is common (mushtarak). It claims that if existence had multiple meanings, then the same thing could be both necessary and contingent, making distinction impossible. The response challenges the underlying assumption. Let's examine the reasoning.

1

Identify the core claim

3
Analyze the response

4

الوجه السادس) لو لم يكن (الوجود معنى واحداً مشتركاً لم يتميز الواجب عن الممكن فإنا إذا قلنا على تقدير كون الوجود معاني متعددة الشيء ( إما أن يجب وجوده أو لا، فقد يجب له الوجود بمعني ولا يجب بمعنى آخر) فيكون الشيء الواحد واجباً ممكناً معاً، فلا يتميز أن أصلاً بخلاف ما إذا كان الوجود معنى واحداً لاستحالة أن تكون نسبة المعنى الواحد إلى شيء واحد بالوجوب، والإمكان معاً بالنظر إلى ذاته ( والجواب ) إن ما ذكرتم مبني على جواز أن يكون لشيء واحد، ملاحظة قوله : (بل يقتضي تصوره أي تصور الشخص المشترك وتقديره وهذا لا ينافي ما قيل: إن الجزئي يمتنع تصور اشتراكه لأنه بمعنى التجويز لا التقدير على ما تقرر في موضعه . قوله : ( ويمكن أن يجاب إلخ حاصله أن اللازم مما ذكر أنه لا بد من معنى واحد عام، يكون آلة لملاحظة تلك الوجودات، وبهذا القدر لا يلزم اشتراك الوجود بالمعنى المتنازع فيه، لجواز أن يكون ذلك المعنى مأخوذاً من الاشتراك اللفظي، بأن يقال : المسمى بالوجود نفس الحقائق والحقائق متخلفة . قوله : (لم يتميز الواجب عن (الممكن أي بالذات خص الممكن بوجود التميز عن الممتنع لكونه مسلوباً عنه جميع الوجودات . قوله : ( فقد يجب له الوجود سواء كان الوجود نفس الحقيقة أو زائداً عليه فإنه يجب ثبوت ماهية الشيء له، وما يقتضيه ذاته ولا يجب له ما عداهما . قوله : ( إن ما ذكرتم إلخ لأن مجرد كونه لا يجب له الوجود بمعنى آخر لا يقتضي كونه ممكناً ما لم يعتبر معه جواز ذلك المعنى له وهو مبني على جواز أن يكون لشيء واحد قوله : ( يقتضي تصوره لا يخلو عن مخالفة لما ذكر في المنطق من أن الجزئي الحقيقي يمتنع فرض اشتراكه فليتأمل . يجب له قوله : ( الوجه السادس إلخ) فيه بحث لأن الواجب ما يجب له وجود ما والممكن ما لا فالامتياز ظاهر بلا إشكال، إلا أن يرجع إلى أن هذه القسمة أيضاً عقلية وجود أصلاً والحصر فيما ذكرته بملاحظة اللفظ وأوضاعه . قوله : ( وكون الشيء الواحد له وجودان إلخ قيل : يفهم منه إبطال الفعلية أعني أن يكون للشيء وجودان بالفعل والفعلية أخص من الإمكان الذي يكفي في جريان الوجه السادس ونفي
(The sixth aspect:) If existence were not a single common meaning, then the Necessary would not be distinguished from the contingent. For if we say, on the assumption that existence has multiple meanings, the thing (is either that its existence is necessary or not), then its existence is necessary in one sense and not necessary in another sense, so the same thing would be necessary and contingent together, so it would not be distinguished at all. Unlike if existence is a single meaning, because it is impossible for the relation of a single meaning to one thing in terms of necessity and possibility together with respect to its essence. (The answer:) What you have mentioned is based on the permissibility of one thing having... Remark. His statement: (Rather, it entails conceiving him) i.e., conceiving the common person and supposing him, and this does not contradict what is said: that the particular is impossible to conceive as shared, because it means possibility, not supposition, as established in its place. His statement: (And it can also be answered etc.) Its summary is that what is necessary from what is mentioned is that there must be a single general meaning that is an instrument for observing those existences, and to this extent the commonness of existence in the disputed sense does not follow, because it is possible that that meaning is taken from verbal commonness, by saying: that which is called existence is the realities themselves, and the realities are different. His statement: (The Necessary is not distinguished from the contingent) i.e., by essence. He specified the contingent by having distinction from the impossible because it is denied all existences. His statement: (For its existence may be necessary) whether existence is the essence itself or superadded to it, for the existence of the thing's essence is necessary for it, and what its essence necessitates, and what is other than these is not necessary for it. His statement: (What you have mentioned etc.) because merely that existence is not necessary for it in another sense does not entail that it is contingent unless the permissibility of that sense for it is also considered, and this is based on the permissibility of one thing having... His statement: (It entails conceiving him) is not devoid of contradiction to what is mentioned in logic that a true particular is impossible to suppose as shared, so reflect. It is necessary for him. His statement: (The sixth aspect etc.) There is discussion in it because the Necessary is that whose existence is necessary for it, and the contingent is that whose existence is not, so distinction is apparent without difficulty, unless it is reduced to the fact that this division is also rational... existence at all, and the confinement in what you mentioned is by considering the word and its usages. His statement: (And that one thing has two existences etc.) It is said: It implies the nullification of actuality, meaning that the thing has two existences in actuality, and actuality is more specific than possibility, which suffices for the application of the sixth aspect and the negation...
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument (al-wajh al-sadis) that if existence were not a single common meaning, the Necessary (wajib) and the contingent (mumkin) would not be distinguished. The reasoning: if existence has multiple meanings, then something could be necessary in one sense and not necessary in another, making it both necessary and contingent simultaneously, which is impossible. But if existence is one meaning, it cannot relate to something as both necessary and possible with respect to its essence. The response argues that this is based on the assumption that one thing can have multiple existence-aspects. The commentary then breaks down various statements from the original text. It clarifies that a negative proposition only requires conceiving the subject, and it suggests an alternative answer: that the single meaning needed is merely a verbal commonality (ishtirak lafzi), not a real one. The commentary also discusses the distinction between Necessary and contingent, noting that contingency is defined by the lacking of existence, and that necessity is determined by essence. It questions the sixth argument, suggesting that distinguishing necessary from contingent is already clear without assuming a single meaning of existence, unless one considers the division as a rational (aql) and verbal matter. The passage ends with a remark that having two actual existences for one thing would nullify actuality, which is more specific than possibility.

Key Takeaway
The sixth argument contends that distinguishing the Necessary from the contingent necessitates a single common meaning of existence, but the response shows this only holds if one assumes a thing can have multiple existence-meanings.

The Second Proof: Existence Cannot Be an Attribute
A reductio proof that existence is not additional to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that existence cannot be an additional attribute of essence, because it would lead to an infinite regress or circularity.

Core Idea
If existence were an attribute, it would need a prior existence—an absurdity.

The author now presents a second, more subtle proof that existence is not an extra property added to essence. This proof uses a conditional chain to show that treating existence as an attribute leads to a logical contradiction. As you read, follow the steps carefully: each 'if' builds on the previous one until the conclusion becomes unavoidable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the logical connectors: 'فلو', 'وإذا', 'فإن'.
The argument is tightly structured; each clause depends on the previous.
2
Identify the main premise
The passage begins with a general principle: any positive attribute subsisting in a thing depends on the thing's own existence. Ensure you understand this claim.
This premise is accepted by both sides.
3
Trace the conditional chain
Follow the 'if... then...' steps: if existence is an attribute, then it subsists in essence, then that subsistence requires a prior existence of the essence, leading to a regress or circularity.
Each step is logically necessary.
4
Understand the absurdities
The conclusion lists three impossible consequences: the thing existing twice, existence preceding itself, or infinite regress. Grasp why each is impossible.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
5
Apply the argument
Consider a concrete essence (e.g., humanity). Try to apply the reasoning to see why its existence cannot be an attribute.
Think: what would 'humanity' be before it has existence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني قيام الصفة الثبوتية بالشيء فرع وجوده ) أي وجود ذلك الشيء ( في نفسه ضرورة) فإن ما لا ثبوت له في نفسه لم يمكن أن يتصف بصفة ثبوتية ولا شك أن الوجود أمر ثبوتي ( فلو كان الوجود صفة زائدة على الماهية لكان قائماً بها، وإذا كان قائماً بها لكان فرعاً على وجودها في نفسها، وإذا كان فرعاً لوجودها في نفسها كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها ينتج لو كان الوجود زائداً على الماهية كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها والتالي باطل لأنه يلزم كون الشيء موجوداً مرتين وتقدم الوجود على نفسه أو التسلسل فكذا المقدم فثبت أن الوجود ليس زائدا في شيء من الماهيات .
The second (aspect: the subsistence of a positive attribute in a thing is derivative from its existence), i.e., the existence of that thing (in itself necessarily), for that which has no subsistence in itself cannot be described by a positive attribute, and there is no doubt that existence is something positive. So if existence were an attribute additional to the essence, it would be subsistent in it; and if it were subsistent in it, it would be derivative from its existence in itself; and if it were derivative from its existence in itself, then the essence would have an existence before its existence. This yields: if existence were additional to the essence, the essence would have an existence before its existence. The consequent is false because it entails the thing being existent twice and the priority of existence over itself, or an infinite regress. Thus the antecedent is false, so it is established that existence is not additional in any of the essences.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents a core argument against the view that existence is an additional attribute of essence. The author states the second proof: the subsistence of any positive attribute in a thing depends on the thing's own existence. Since existence itself is positive, if it were an attribute, it would need to subsist in the essence. But that subsistence would require the essence to already exist, leading to a vicious circle: the essence would need an existence before its existence. This is absurd, as it implies the thing exists twice, or the existence precedes itself, or an infinite regress. Therefore, existence cannot be an attribute; it must be identical to the essence or a part of it. The passage follows a clear logical structure: premise, conditional reasoning, and reduction to absurdity.

Key Terms

وجود
ماهية
قيام
فرع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument is circular because it assumes existence is needed for attribution, but the attribute existence itself is what is being examined. However, the argument's premise is about any attribute, not existence specifically, so it is not circular.
Correction: The premise applies to all positive attributes equally. It does not presuppose the conclusion; it uses a general principle to derive a contradiction.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if existence were an additional attribute of essence?
A) The essence would be non-existent.
B) The essence would have an existence before its existence.
C) The attribute would be negative.
D) The essence would be impossible.

Key Takeaway
Existence cannot be an attribute of essence because that would force a vicious regress; existence is therefore either identical to essence or a constituent of it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Resolving the Objection of Obtaining the Obtained
Objection and response on joining existence to an existent essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical objection known as 'obtaining the obtained' (تحصيل الحاصل) and how the author resolves it by distinguishing between different respects of obtaining.

Core Idea
Obtaining the obtained is only impossible if the obtaining is identical in every respect.

This lesson examines a classic objection to the theory that existence joins the essence. The objector presents a dilemma: either existence joins at the time of existence (leading to obtaining the obtained) or at the time of non-existence (leading to contradiction). The author's response is subtle but crucial for understanding how kalam thinkers defend their metaphysical principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the dilemma presented: if existence joins when the essence is already existent, it seems to be obtaining what is already obtained, which is deemed absurd.
The objection is based on the principle that an already existent thing cannot be brought into existence again.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The objection has two alternatives: either the joining occurs at the time of existence (leading to 'obtaining the obtained') or at the time of non-existence (leading to 'conjunction of contradictories'). Note the logical problem with each.
The second horn is impossible because existence and non-existence cannot coexist.
3
See how the author chooses the first horn
The author selects the first alternative and denies that 'obtaining the obtained' is universally impossible. He distinguishes between obtaining something that was already obtained before this obtaining and obtaining something through a new act.
The key move: the new act of obtaining brings about a different instance or aspect.
4
Understand the distinction that resolves the problem
The author argues that the impossibility only applies when the obtaining is of what is already obtained prior to this obtaining. Since the new existence is a different 'this existence', it is not a repetition of the same.
This distinction avoids the absurdity and saves the theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بل) في زمان كونها موجودة بهذا الوجود إضراب عن مضمون العبارة وفيه إشارة إلى دفع ما قيل : إن انضمام الوجود إن كان في زمان الوجود يلزم تحصيل الحاصل وإن كان في زمان العدم يلزم اجتماع النقيضين وحاصل الدفع اختيار الشق الأول، ومنع استحالة تحصيل الحاصل لأنه تحصيل للحاصل بهذا التحصيل وذا ليس بمحال إنما المحال تحصيل ما هو حاصل قبل هذا التحصيل.
His saying: '(but) at the time of its being existent with this existence' is a digression from the content of the expression, and in it there is an indication of repelling what was said: that if the joining of existence occurs at the time of existence, it entails obtaining the obtained; and if at the time of non-existence, it entails the conjunction of two contradictories. The gist of the repulsion is choosing the first alternative and denying the impossibility of obtaining the obtained, because it is obtaining the obtained by this obtaining, and that is not impossible; rather, the impossible is obtaining what is obtained before this obtaining.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage deals with an objection to the view that existence joins the essence. The objection says: if existence joins the essence when the essence is already existent, that is 'obtaining the obtained' (تحصيل الحاصل), which is absurd; if it joins when the essence is non-existent, then existence and non-existence would coexist, which is contradictory. The author responds by choosing the first alternative and denying that obtaining the obtained is inherently impossible. He argues that the existence that joins is a specific existence (this existence), and the essence's prior existence is a different existence. So it is not obtaining what is already obtained in the same respect; it is a new instantiation. Thus, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
تحصيل الحاصل
اجتماع النقيضين
انضمام الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Obtaining the obtained is always logically impossible.
Correction: It is only impossible if the obtaining is of what is already obtained before that obtaining; a new obtaining of the same thing is possible if it is a different respect or instance.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the objection that adding existence to an already existent essence is 'obtaining the obtained'?
A) He denies that the essence already exists.
B) He argues that obtaining the obtained is not impossible in this context because it is a different obtaining.
C) He accepts the objection and modifies the theory.
D) He claims the objection is based on a misunderstanding of time.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of obtaining the obtained only applies when the obtaining is of the same thing in the same respect, not when a new act brings about a different instantiation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed an idea as impossible without examining whether it truly is the same as what you've dismissed before? Think of a time you stubbornly rejected a new perspective because it seemed like 'obtaining the obtained'. How will you change your approach now that you understand the distinction?
?
The author shows that 'this existence' is a new specific existence. How does this truth about God's creation being new each moment challenge your daily awareness of His constant creative activity? Will you live today with the freshness of seeing each moment as a new existence from Him?
?
The objection seemed logically airtight, but was resolved by a subtle distinction. What assumptions do you hold about God that you have not critically examined? Are you willing to scrutinize them as the author does here?

The Three Impossibilities from the Regress Argument
The author lists three absurd consequences of existence being an attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three logical impossibilities that arise if existence is considered an attribute of the essence, and the specific assumptions under which each occurs.

Core Idea
Three distinct impossibilities arise from the regress argument, each based on a different logical assumption.

This passage delves into the logical structure of the regress argument against existence being an attribute. The author clarifies that the statement about priority of a thing over itself is not part of the direct conclusion but an additional consequence. He then enumerates three separate impossibilities that would follow, showing the precision of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the technical discussion.
Pay attention to the logical connectors.
2
Identify the three impossibilities
Locate the three enumerated impossibilities and note the conditions under which each applies.
The first is unconditional, the second assumes identity, the third assumes otherness.
3
Understand the logical structure
Observe how the author distinguishes between the apodosis and the conjoined consequent.
4
Reflect on the use of 'and'
Consider why the author uses 'and' between the second and third impossibilities rather than 'or'.
They share a common ordering, even though each arises from a different assumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فيلزم إلخ) يعني أن قوله ويلزم تقدم الشيء على نفسه ليس في حيز الجزاء، وإلا لكان الواجب أن يقول وتقدم الشيء على نفسه أو لزوم تقدم الشيء على نفسه، بل هو معطوف على مقدر لازم من التالي لزوماً بيناً، ولذا تركه المصنف فالأمور الثلاثة محالات لازمة للتالي مترتبة عليه، أما الأول فمن القبلية مع قطع النظر عن كون الوجود السابق عين اللاحق أو غيره والثاني على تقدير العينية والثالث على تقدير الغيرية، وإنما أورد الواو بين الثاني والثالث نظراً إلى اجتماعهما في الترتيب على كون الوجود السابق قبل اللاحق وإن كان لزوم كل واحد منهما على تقدير مباين لتقدير الآخر، وبهذا الاعتبار يصح أن يكون موقعاً لأو، كما سيجيء في عبارة الشارح.
His saying: 'so it entails, etc.' means that his saying 'and the priority of a thing over itself' is not in the position of the apodosis; otherwise he would have had to say 'and the priority of a thing over itself' or 'the necessity of the priority of a thing over itself.' Rather, it is conjoined to an implied [consequent] that is a necessary concomitant of the consequent. Therefore, the author omitted it. So the three impossibilities are necessary concomitants of the consequent, arranged in order: (1) the first is from priority, regardless of whether the prior existence is identical to the posterior or other; (2) the second on the assumption of identity; (3) the third on the assumption of otherness. He only used 'and' between the second and third because they both share in the ordering that the prior existence is before the posterior, even though the occurrence of each is based on a different assumption. In this respect, 'or' could also be used, as will come in the commentator's statement.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage clarifies the logical structure of the regress argument. The author explains that the statement 'and the priority of a thing over itself' is not part of the direct result; it is an additional consequence. He then enumerates three distinct impossibilities that would follow if existence were an attribute: (1) the essence would have a prior existence (being existent twice), (2) if the prior existence is identical to the posterior, then the thing would be prior to itself, (3) if the prior existence is different, then an infinite regress occurs. The commentator notes that the use of 'and' between the second and third is because they are both based on the ordering of priority, even though each stems from a different assumption. This careful articulation shows the precision of the argument.

Key Terms
محال
تقدم الشيء على نفسه
عينية
غيرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the three impossibilities are all the same or that they arise under the same condition.
Correction: Each impossibility applies under a specific condition: the first is unconditional, the second assumes the prior existence is identical to the posterior, and the third assumes they are different.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on what assumption does the impossibility of the thing being prior to itself occur?
A) When the prior existence is different from the posterior.
B) When the prior existence is identical to the posterior.
C) Regardless of identity or difference.
D) Only if there is an infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
The three impossibilities from the regress argument are precisely distinguished based on whether the prior existence is identical to or different from the posterior.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson demonstrates that even a subtle logical misstep about God's existence leads to absurdity. Have you ever held a simplified or contradictory view about Allah's attributes without realizing its logical consequences? How does this precision challenge you to be more careful in your aqeedah?
?
If the necessity of Allah's existence is so absolute that it cannot be a mere attribute, does your worship consistently reflect that? Do you sometimes treat Allah as a 'quality' added to your life rather than the Necessarily Existent upon Whom everything depends? What would change if you fully internalized this today?

The Infinite Regress: What It Is and Why It Is Impossible
The author defines the infinite regress and asserts its impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific concept of infinite regress that is considered impossible in kalam and the reasoning behind its impossibility.

Core Idea
An actual infinite series of dependent existences is impossible.

The author begins by clarifying the exact meaning of the infinite regress under discussion, distinguishing it from a merely endless sequence. He then states that an actual infinite series is impossible. Understanding this distinction is crucial before moving to the argument that uses this impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's precise wording: 'سلسلة في الوجودات الغير المتناهية المترتبة المجتمعة' – an actual infinite series of ordered, simultaneous existences.
The author emphasizes 'بالفعل' (actual) to avoid confusion with potential infinity.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two interrelated claims: (1) that such a regress is entailed under a certain assumption, and (2) that this actual infinite series is impossible. Find where each is stated.
The impossibility is the cornerstone: 'إنما المحال وجود السلسلة الغير المتناهية بالفعل'.
3
Reflect on why it is impossible
Ask yourself: why would an actual infinite series of dependent existences be impossible? The author does not elaborate here, but hints are given in the next lesson. For now, accept it as a settled position in kalam.
Later lessons will show the consequences of assuming such a regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وتتسلسل الوجودات إلخ) أي يلزم وجود سلسلة في الوجودات الغير المتناهية المترتبة المجتمعة لكون كل وجود سابق شرطاً لوجود لاحق، لا أنه يلزم أن لا تنتهي الوجودات إلى غير النهاية حتى يقال : إنه ليس بمحال إنما المحال وجود السلسلة الغير المتناهية بالفعل . قوله: (ومع) امتناعه فلا بد إلخ) أي مع امتناع التسلسل في نفس الأمر لو فرض وجوده هاهنا فالمطلوب وهو كون الوجود نفس الماهية ثابت لأن جميع الوجودات المتسلسلة الغير المتناهية، بحيث لا يشذ منها وجود مجموع مغاير لكل واحد من الوجودات بالذات، لوجوب مغايرة الكل مع الجزء، فالكل من حيث الكل ليس نفس الماهية ، ولا جزءاً منها فهو خارج عنها قائم بها كقيام كل واحد منها، فيكون قيامه فرعاً لوجود الماهية في نفسها لما مر، ولا يكون ذلك الوجود زائداً على الماهية وإلا لم يكن جميع ما فرضناه جميعاً، فيكون نفسها وهو المطلوب فتدبر، فإنه تقرير منقح يتضح به المرام ولا يرد عليه الشكوك التي عرضت للناظرين في هذا المقام.
His saying: 'and existences form an infinite regress, etc.' means that a series of infinite, ordered, simultaneous existences is entailed, because each prior existence is a condition for a posterior existence. It does not mean that the existences do not end at infinity, such that one could say: that is not impossible; rather, the impossible is the existence of an actual infinite series. His saying: 'and with its impossibility, there is no alternative, etc.' means: with the impossibility of the regress in reality, if its existence were assumed here, then the required conclusion, i.e., that existence is identical to essence, is established. Because all the infinite sequential existences (such that no existence is omitted) have a sum that is essentially distinct from each individual existence, due to the necessary difference between the whole and the part. So the whole, qua whole, is neither the essence nor a part of it; it is external to it, subsisting in it, like the subsistence of each individual one. Thus, its subsistence is derivative from the existence of the essence in itself, as mentioned. And that existence (i.e., the whole) is not additional to the essence; otherwise, the sum of what we assumed would not be the sum. So it is the essence itself, and that is the conclusion. So reflect, for it is a refined exposition that clarifies the objective, and the doubts that have occurred to the examiners in this context do not apply to it.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses the infinite regress argument. The author clarifies that the regress in question is an actual infinite series of existences, each dependent on a prior one. Such an actual infinite is impossible. Then, assuming for argument that such a regress could exist, the author shows that the sum of all these existences would be something distinct from each individual existence. This sum, being a whole, cannot be identical to the essence nor a part of it; it would be an additional attribute subsisting in the essence. But if it were additional, it would require a prior existence, leading to an infinite regress. Since the only way to stop the regress is that existence is not additional but identical to the essence, the conclusion holds. The author claims this refined exposition avoids the doubts that have troubled scholars.

Key Terms
تسلسل
غير متناهية
بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any infinite regress is impossible, but here only an actual infinite series of simultaneous existences is impossible; a potential infinite (like numbers) is not.
Correction: The text explicitly says: 'لا أنه يلزم أن لا تنتهي الوجودات إلى غير النهاية حتى يقال : إنه ليس بمحال' – it does not mean the existences do not end at infinity (which is not impossible). The impossible is the actual infinite series.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of infinite series is considered impossible?
A) A potential infinite series
B) An actual infinite series (السلسلة الغير المتناهية بالفعل)
C) Any infinite regress
D) A series that ends at infinity

Key Takeaway
The impossible regress is an actual infinite series of simultaneous, ordered existences, not a potential infinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on an endless chain of excuses or justifications to avoid facing the ultimate reality of your dependence on Allah? What would it mean for you to stop the regress and admit that only He is self-sufficient?
?
The author distinguishes between a potential infinite and an actual infinite. In your own life, what 'infinite' pursuits (money, status, pleasures) are you chasing as if they could be actually attained—and how does this lesson expose the impossibility of ever reaching a final goal without Allah?
?
If the existence of this actual infinite series is impossible, then every chain of dependency must terminate in a Self-Sufficient Being. Can you honestly point to one area of your life where you still live as though something other than Allah is your ultimate support—and what step will you take today to break that chain?

From Regress to Identity: Existence is the Essence
The author argues that even assuming an infinite regress, the sum of existences must be identical to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how assuming an infinite regress leads to the conclusion that existence is identical to essence, not an added attribute.

Core Idea
If existence were additional to essence, it would require an infinite regress; only identity stops the regress.

After establishing the impossibility of an actual infinite regress, the author now presents a powerful argument: even if such a regress were assumed, the sum of all existences would be distinct from each part, forcing us to accept that existence is not additional but identical to essence. This is a refined exposition that avoids common doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic from 'ومع امتناعه' to the end, with translation. The argument is intricate; read slowly.
Underline key terms: مجموع, كل, جزء.
2
Trace the logic about the sum
Identify the three claims: (a) the sum of all existences is distinct from each individual existence, (b) the whole (sum) is external to the essence and subsists in it, (c) if the sum were additional, it would require a prior existence, leading to regress.
The author uses 'قيام' (subsistence) – the whole subsists in the essence like each individual does.
3
Conclude the argument
The conclusion: the sum cannot be additional to essence, so it must be identical to essence. That is the required conclusion: existence (the sum) is the essence itself.
The author says 'فيكون نفسها وهو المطلوب' – so it is the essence itself, and that is what was sought.

Proof That Existence Is Identical to Essence
Proof that existence is identical to essence via infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof from infinite regress that existence cannot be an additional attribute to essence and must be identical to it.

Core Idea
If existence were added to essence, infinite regress would follow, so existence must be identical to essence.

This lesson presents the first part of the argument concerning the relationship between existence and essence. The author demonstrates that if existence were a separate attribute, it would require another existence, leading to an endless chain — an impossibility. Thus, existence must be identical to essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall argument. Then read the translation.
Notice the tight logical sequence.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument assumes that if existence is additional to essence, it must itself have an existence to subsist in, leading to a third existence.
3
Follow the regress
Trace how this leads to an endless chain of existences. Understand why such a regress is considered impossible.
The impossibility is a foundational principle in kalam.
4
Reach the conclusion
Since the regress is impossible, there must be an existence that is not additional to essence – that existence is identical to essence.
This is the desired conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيام هذا الوجود بها وجود ثالث وتتسلسل الوجودات إلى ما لا نهاية له وهو ممتنع ومع امتناعه فلا بد هناك من وجود لا يكون بينه وبين الماهية وجود آخر قطعاً)، ) فيكون هو عين الماهية وذلك لأن جميع هذه الوجودات الزائدة التي لا تتناهى عارضة للماهية، فتقتضي أن يكون لها وجود قبلها لامتناع اتصاف المعدوم بالصفات الثبوتية، وذلك الوجود لا يكون زائداً على الماهية وإلا لم يكن ما فرضناه جميعاً جميعاً، بل يكون عينها وهو المطلوب ) والجواب أن الضرورة ) التي ادعيتموها إنما هي ( في صفة وجودية هي غير الوجود فإن البديهة تشهد بأن كل صفة ثبوتية سوى الوجود، فإن قيامها بالموصوف فرع وجود الموصوف في نفسه (وأما الوجود التعارض من خواص الأدلة وإنما قيد بذلك لأن التخصيص بسبب المعارض تخصيص للحكم مع جريان الدليل فيما خص عن الحكم الكلي، وهو يدل على بطلان دليل ذلك الحكم وانتقاضه كما فيما نحن فيه، ولذا جعل الدليل المعارض سبباً للتخصيص فقال : لما ذكرتم بخلاف التخصيص بسبب عدم جريان الدليل، فإنه جار في الأحكام العقلية كقولهم نقيضا المتساويين متساويان خص منه الأمور الشاملة لعدم جريان الدليل فيه لا بسبب وجود المعارض وقس على هذا. قوله: (الضرورة إلخ) لما لم يخص المستدل القيام بكونه في الخارج بل أطلقه وقيد الصفة بالثبوتية أجاب الشارح بأنه إن أراد بالثبوتية الموجودة في الخارج فمسلم أن قيامها يقتضي وجود الموصوف في الخارج لكن الوجود ليس كذلك، وإن أراد بهما ليس السلب في مفهومه، فلا نسلم أن قيامها مطلقاً يقتضي وجود الموصوف فيه، بل إذا كان القيام خارجياً، وقيام الوجود بالماهية ليس كذلك، بل في العقل، فلا يلزم أن يكون للماهية قبل وجودها في الخارج وجود فيه حتى يلزم المحالات وبما حررنا لك اندفع ما قيل أن الضرورية حاكمة بأن الصفة بالموصوف فرع وجود الموصوف سواء كانت موجودة أو معدومة نحو زيد أعمى فالتخصيص
قوله : ( ولقائل أن يقول إلخ) قيل : إذا كان الفارق هو الضرورة العقلية أيضاً، لم يكن من قبيل التخصيص المذكور
١٣٢
للأحكام العقلية اليقينية بسبب ما يعارضها كما هو دأب أصحاب العلوم الظنية في أحكامها العامة فلايصح قطعا بل الصواب أن يقال : الضرورة تحكم بأن كل صفة ثبوتية أي موجودة في الخارج فإن قيامها بالموصوف فرع وجوده فيه، وليس الوجود بالموجودة لا وجه له لأن ذلك إنما هو على تقدير كون القيام في الخارج، ومقصود الشارح أن القيام مطلقاً إنما يقتضي وجود الموصوف في الخارج إذا كانت الصفة موجودة في الخارج. قوله : ( وليس الوجود إلخ) إذ ليس في الخارج ماهية وجود يقوم بها كالسواد والجسم . قوله : (بل امتيازه إلخ) يعني أنه إذا حصل الهوية الخارجية حللها العقل إلى ماهية ووجود بالنظر إلى ترتب الآثار عليها ويصفها به فاتصافها به اتصاف ذهني انتزاعي، وهو يقتضي إلا كون الماهية في الخارج بحيث ينتزع العقل الوجود منها، فلا يرد أنه لو كان الاتصاف به في العقل يلزم احتياج الموجودات الخارجية في كونها موجودة إلى العقل، وذلك بين البطلان فإن الأشياء موجودة في الخارج مع قطع النظر عن وجود ذهن وعقل، ويلزم احتياج الواجب في وجوده إلى وجود الذهن لأن ذلك، إنما يلزم إذا كان الاتصاف به في الذهن حقيقياً لا انتزاعياً، وكذا لا يرد أنه يلزم التسلسل في الوجودات الذهنية لأن الاتصاف به في الذهن يكون فرعاً لوجود الماهية في الذهن، وتنقل الكلام إلى الوجود الثاني والثالث والرابع وهكذا، لأن هذا التسلسل في الأمور الاعتبارية التي تنقطع باعتبار العقل فتدبر فإنه دقيق قد أطال الفضلاء فيه الكلام، وما فازوا بالمرام وكذا لا يرد ما أورده بعض الفضلاء من أن في القول بامتيازهما في العقل اعترافاً بمذهب الشيخ فكيف يكون جواباً لاستدلاله لأن مذهبه أنه ليس ما يصدق عليه الوجود أمراً وراء الحقيقة، فالوجود في الخارج والعقل نفس الحقيقة والتغاير بينهما باعتبار المفهوم، وهذا المجيب يقول: إن ما يصدق عليه الوجود أمر مغاير للماهية في الذهن وليس مغايراً لها في الخارج، نعم لو حمل مذهب الشيخ على أن مراده نفي الزيادة في الخارج كما يدل عليه أدلته على ما يحققه المصنف، كان في الجواب المذكور اعترافاً لمذهبه . قوله : (بل الصواب أن يقال : إلخ) فإن قلت : على هذا بطل الفرق الذي ذكروه بين السالبة والموجبة بأن السالبة لا تقتضي وجود الموضوع بخلاف الموجبة، للدلالة على أن المحمول في الموجبة إذا لم يكن موجوداً خارجياً لا يقتضي وجود الموضوع، قلت: المنفي هاهنا في المآل هو القيام الخارجي المقتضي لتقدم الوجود الخارجي والمدعى في الموجبة هو اقتضاء وجود الموضوع حال اعتبار الحكم مطلقاً فلا منافاة، قال بعض المحققين الظاهر أن مراده أن الصواب في جواب دليل الشيخ أن يقال : كذا وليس بصحيح لأن هذا عين مذهب الشيخ وهو أن الوجود ليس زائداً في الخارج، بل في العقل إذ لو كان زائداً في الخارج لزم المحالات، وقد سلم هذا فكيف يكون جواباً عنه وهذا يوافق ما في شرح حكمة العين من أن النزاع في زيادته بحسب الخارج لكن قال الشارح في حواشيه : الظاهر أن النزاع في كونه زائدا في نفس الأمر، وبحسب الذهن بحسب الخارج، وبهذا صرح أفضل المحققين في تجريده حيث قال : فزيادته في التصور . لا
The subsistence of this existence in it is a third existence, and the existences would be endless, which is impossible. Given its impossibility, there must necessarily be an existence such that there is no other existence between it and the essence, so it is identical to the essence. That is because all these additional existences which are endless are accidents of the essence, and they require that the essence have an existence prior to them because it is impossible for the non-existent to be described with positive attributes. That existence cannot be additional to the essence; otherwise, our assumption would not be complete; rather, it is identical to it — that is what is sought. The answer: the necessity that you claimed is only in a positive attribute that is not existence, for intuition testifies that every positive attribute other than existence, its subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described itself. As for existence, necessity in it is the opposite, because it necessitates the impossibility of its being preceded by existence due to what you mentioned of the requiredness of the thing being existent twice, and the requiredness of the thing preceding itself, or the endlessness of existences. And one may say: this answer is a kind of specification (takhṣīṣ). But [the objection fails] because the meaning of his saying: ('because all these additional endless existences' i.e. actually endless, as you know) is refuted by what is in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid: we do not grant that upon the assumption of [endless] succession, an actual infinite totality is realized, but rather any totality assumed is accidental by means of another accidental existence, because this succession is the lack of ending of existences to an existence beyond which there is no existence between it and the essence. His saying: ('due to what is contrary to them') i.e. due to what is contrary to their posit from intuition and evidence, for contradiction is specific to proofs. He restricts it thus because specification due to a contrary is a specification of the judgment while the evidence remains in what is excluded from the universal judgment, and it indicates the falsity of the evidence of that judgment and its dissolution, as here. That is why he made the contrary evidence a reason for specification, saying: 'as you mentioned, unlike specification due to the evidence's lack of applicability, for that is valid in rational judgments like their saying: two equals are equal, from which is excluded universal matters because the evidence does not apply in them, not due to a contrary evidence.' So analogize. His saying: ('the necessity etc.') Since the arguer did not specify that the subsistence is external but rather left it unrestricted and restricted the attribute to positive, the commentator answered: if by 'positive' he means existing externally, then it is accepted that its subsistence requires the existence of the described externally, but existence is not so. If he means that negation is not in its concept, then we do not accept that its subsistence absolutely requires the existence of the described in it, but rather if the subsistence is external. The subsistence of existence in the essence is not so; rather, it is mental. Thus it is not necessary that the essence have an existence prior to its external existence to avoid the impossibilities. And by what we have refined for you, what was said — that the intuitive judgment that the attribute's subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described whether it is existent or non-existent, like 'Zayd is blind', so the specification [is invalid] — is repelled. His saying: ('and one may say etc.') It was said: if the differentiator is also rational intuition, then it is not a specification of the mentioned kind. For rational certain judgments are not specified due to what is contrary to them, as is the practice of practitioners of conjectural sciences in their universal judgments, absolutely not valid. Rather the correct thing to say is: the rational necessity rules that every positive attribute, i.e. existing externally, its subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described therein, but existence is not such. The statement 'not existence as an existent' has no basis, because that is only on the assumption that the subsistence is external. The commentator's intent is that subsistence absolutely requires the existence of the described externally only if the attribute is external. His saying: ('and existence is not etc.') because there is no essence in the external for existence to subsist in it, like blackness and body. His saying: ('rather their distinctness etc.') means that when the external identity is realized, the mind analyzes it into essence and existence with respect to the ordering of effects upon them and describes it with it, so its description with it is a mental, abstractive description. This requires that the essence be external such that the mind extracts existence from it. Thus it is not objected that if the description were mental, then external existents would need the mind to be existent — that is obviously false, for things exist externally irrespective of mind and reason. Nor would it require the Necessary to need the mind for Its existence, because that would only follow if the description were real, not abstractive. Similarly, it is not objected that it leads to an endless succession of mental existences, because the connection is in, but rather the description with it in the mind is dependent on the mind, and the discourse moves to the second, third, fourth existence, etc., because this succession is in the mental considerations that are terminated by the mind's consideration. So ponder, for it is subtle; the learned have extended speech on it and have not attained the goal. Also not objected what some scholars presented: that in the statement of their distinctness in the mind there is an admission to the doctrine of the Shaykh (al-Rāzī), so how could it be an answer to his proof? For his doctrine is that what the existence is predicated of is nothing beyond the reality; rather, existence in the external and the mind is the reality itself, and the difference between them is in concept. But this answerer says: what existence is predicated of is something distinct from the essence in the mind but not distinct from it in the external. Yes, if the Shaykh's doctrine is interpreted as denying [existence's] being additional in the external (as his proofs indicate, according to the author's verification), then the answer admits his doctrine. His saying: ('rather the correct thing to say etc.') It might be said: on this view, the distinction made between negative and positive propositions — that the negative does not require the existence of the subject unlike the positive — is nullified, because it indicates that the predicate in the positive, if not externally existent, does not require the existence of the subject. I say: what is negated here ultimately is the external subsistence which requires the precedence of external existence, while what is claimed in the positive is the requirement of the subject's existence in the state of considering the judgment absolutely, so there is no conflict. Some investigators said: It seems that his intent is that the correct answer to the Shaykh's proof is to say thus, but it is not correct because this is exactly the Shaykh's doctrine — that existence is not additional externally but rather mentally; if it were additional externally, impossibilities would follow. And he has admitted this, so how can it be an answer? This agrees with what is in Sharḥ Ḥikmat al-ʿAyn that the dispute is about its being additional in the external, but the commentator said in his glosses: Apparently the dispute is about its being additional in reality, and in relation to the mind is according to the external. And the most excellent of investigators stated this in his Tajrīd where he said: 'So its additionalness in conception. No.'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a complete dialectical argument about the relationship between existence (wujud) and essence (mahiyya) — specifically, the claim that existence is not something added to essence but is either identical to it or a part of it. The passage begins with a proof: if existence were additional to essence, then there would have to be another existence for that additional existence to subsist in, leading to an infinite regress of existences. Since such a regress is impossible, there must be an existence with no intermediary between it and essence — that existence is identical to essence. The proof then points out that the regress of additional existences would require a prior existence for the essence because a non-existent cannot have positive attributes. That prior existence cannot be additional; otherwise the assumption of a final regress would fail; it must be identical to essence. 

The answer from the defender of the additionalness of existence is that the necessity claimed only applies to positive attributes other than existence. Intuitive reason testifies that every positive attribute besides existence requires the prior existence of the subject; but existence itself is the opposite: existence cannot be preceded by another existence, because that would make the thing existent twice, or involve self-precedence, or lead to infinite regress. Thus existence is unique among attributes in not requiring a prior existence. 

Then an objection is raised: this answer is a case of 'takhsis' (specifying a universal rational judgment with an exception), which is not allowed in certain rational judgments. The commentary enters into a detailed discussion about the nature of takhsis: it is permissible when a conflicting evidence is present, but not when the evidence simply does not apply. The commentator (al-Jurjani) explains that the specification here is based on the fact that existence is different from other attributes in its necessity. He refutes a counter-objection by distinguishing between external subsistence and mental subsistence: the necessity of a prior existence only applies when the attribute subsists externally; but existence subsists mentally, not externally, so no regress follows. The commentary then addresses several further objections: that this mental distinction implies that external things need the mind to exist; that it leads to infinite regress in mental existences; and that it admits the Shaykh's (al-Razi's) doctrine rather than answering it. Each objection is refuted: the mental attribution is abstractive, not real; the mental regress is in considerations, not actual; and the Shaykh's real view is about external additionalness, which this answer denies. Finally, the passage corrects a false statement of the 'correct' answer and clarifies the real point of contention: existence is not additional externally, but only conceptually. The entire discussion proceeds through proof, answer, objection, and multiple layers of defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that existence, like other attributes, must be preceded by a prior existence of the subject.
Correction: The passage argues that existence is the first actuality and cannot be preceded by another existence, otherwise an infinite regress results.

Checkpoint
What is the main consequence drawn in the proof if existence were additional to essence?
A) Existence would be unknowable.
B) An infinite regress of existences would follow.
C) Essence would not need existence.
D) Existence would be a mere concept.

Key Takeaway
Existence cannot be an added attribute because that leads to an infinite regress; therefore existence is identical to essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your existence were merely an added attribute to your essence, would you fear losing it? But the proof shows existence is identical to essence—what does that mean for your certainty that you exist, and how does that certainty relate to your certainty in the Necessary Existent?
?
The proof relies on the impossibility of infinite regress. In your own life, do you build your identity on an endless chain of achievements or validations? How does recognizing a foundational existence—one that is not added but essential—challenge you to ground your worth in your essential relationship with Allah?
?
Consider the statement 'a non-existent cannot have positive attributes.' This implies that for you to have any attribute—faith, character, love—you must first exist. Are you living as if your existence is a gracious gift from the Necessary Existent, or do you take it for granted? What would it mean to thank Allah not just for what you have, but for that you are?

Allah's Existence
advanced
10 min
The Answer and the Objection of Specification
Defender's answer and the objection of specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defender's answer that existence alone requires no prior existence and the objection that this answer is an arbitrary specification.

Core Idea
Existence is unique among attributes: it cannot be preceded by another existence, so the regress argument fails.

After presenting the proof that existence is identical to essence, the text turns to the defender of additionalness. The defender argues that the necessity of a prior existence only applies to attributes other than existence. This leads to an objection that such a response is a case of unlawful specification (takhsis) of a rational principle. We explore this exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
First read the answer: the necessity claimed is only for attributes other than existence.
2
Understand the uniqueness of existence
Existence cannot be preceded by another existence, so the regress does not apply to existence itself.
3
Examine the objection
The objector says this answer is a specification (takhsis) of the general rule that every attribute needs a prior subject.
Specification of rational certainties is not allowed.
4
Follow the rebuttal
The commentary rebuts by distinguishing between specification due to contrary evidence and lack of applicability. This is the former.

The subsistence of this existence in it is a third existence, and the existences would be endless, which is impossible. Given its impossibility, there must necessarily be an existence such that there is no other existence between it and the essence, so it is identical to the essence. That is because all these additional existences which are endless are accidents of the essence, and they require that the essence have an existence prior to them because it is impossible for the non-existent to be described with positive attributes. That existence cannot be additional to the essence; otherwise, our assumption would not be complete; rather, it is identical to it — that is what is sought. The answer: the necessity that you claimed is only in a positive attribute that is not existence, for intuition testifies that every positive attribute other than existence, its subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described itself. As for existence, necessity in it is the opposite, because it necessitates the impossibility of its being preceded by existence due to what you mentioned of the requiredness of the thing being existent twice, and the requiredness of the thing preceding itself, or the endlessness of existences. And one may say: this answer is a kind of specification (takhṣīṣ). But [the objection fails] because the meaning of his saying: ('because all these additional endless existences' i.e. actually endless, as you know) is refuted by what is in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid: we do not grant that upon the assumption of [endless] succession, an actual infinite totality is realized, but rather any totality assumed is accidental by means of another accidental existence, because this succession is the lack of ending of existences to an existence beyond which there is no existence between it and the essence. His saying: ('due to what is contrary to them') i.e. due to what is contrary to their posit from intuition and evidence, for contradiction is specific to proofs. He restricts it thus because specification due to a contrary is a specification of the judgment while the evidence remains in what is excluded from the universal judgment, and it indicates the falsity of the evidence of that judgment and its dissolution, as here. That is why he made the contrary evidence a reason for specification, saying: 'as you mentioned, unlike specification due to the evidence's lack of applicability, for that is valid in rational judgments like their saying: two equals are equal, from which is excluded universal matters because the evidence does not apply in them, not due to a contrary evidence.' So analogize. His saying: ('the necessity etc.') Since the arguer did not specify that the subsistence is external but rather left it unrestricted and restricted the attribute to positive, the commentator answered: if by 'positive' he means existing externally, then it is accepted that its subsistence requires the existence of the described externally, but existence is not so. If he means that negation is not in its concept, then we do not accept that its subsistence absolutely requires the existence of the described in it, but rather if the subsistence is external. The subsistence of existence in the essence is not so; rather, it is mental. Thus it is not necessary that the essence have an existence prior to its external existence to avoid the impossibilities. And by what we have refined for you, what was said — that the intuitive judgment that the attribute's subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described whether it is existent or non-existent, like 'Zayd is blind', so the specification [is invalid] — is repelled. His saying: ('and one may say etc.') It was said: if the differentiator is also rational intuition, then it is not a specification of the mentioned kind. For rational certain judgments are not specified due to what is contrary to them, as is the practice of practitioners of conjectural sciences in their universal judgments, absolutely not valid. Rather the correct thing to say is: the rational necessity rules that every positive attribute, i.e. existing externally, its subsistence in the described depends on the existence of the described therein, but existence is not such. The statement 'not existence as an existent' has no basis, because that is only on the assumption that the subsistence is external. The commentator's intent is that subsistence absolutely requires the existence of the described externally only if the attribute is external. His saying: ('and existence is not etc.') because there is no essence in the external for existence to subsist in it, like blackness and body. His saying: ('rather their distinctness etc.') means that when the external identity is realized, the mind analyzes it into essence and existence with respect to the ordering of effects upon them and describes it with it, so its description with it is a mental, abstractive description. This requires that the essence be external such that the mind extracts existence from it. Thus it is not objected that if the description were mental, then external existents would need the mind to be existent — that is obviously false, for things exist externally irrespective of mind and reason. Nor would it require the Necessary to need the mind for Its existence, because that would only follow if the description were real, not abstractive. Similarly, it is not objected that it leads to an endless succession of mental existences, because the connection is in, but rather the description with it in the mind is dependent on the mind, and the discourse moves to the second, third, fourth existence, etc., because this succession is in the mental considerations that are terminated by the mind's consideration. So ponder, for it is subtle; the learned have extended speech on it and have not attained the goal. Also not objected what some scholars presented: that in the statement of their distinctness in the mind there is an admission to the doctrine of the Shaykh (al-Rāzī), so how could it be an answer to his proof? For his doctrine is that what the existence is predicated of is nothing beyond the reality; rather, existence in the external and the mind is the reality itself, and the difference between them is in concept. But this answerer says: what existence is predicated of is something distinct from the essence in the mind but not distinct from it in the external. Yes, if the Shaykh's doctrine is interpreted as denying [existence's] being additional in the external (as his proofs indicate, according to the author's verification), then the answer admits his doctrine. His saying: ('rather the correct thing to say etc.') It might be said: on this view, the distinction made between negative and positive propositions — that the negative does not require the existence of the subject unlike the positive — is nullified, because it indicates that the predicate in the positive, if not externally existent, does not require the existence of the subject. I say: what is negated here ultimately is the external subsistence which requires the precedence of external existence, while what is claimed in the positive is the requirement of the subject's existence in the state of considering the judgment absolutely, so there is no conflict. Some investigators said: It seems that his intent is that the correct answer to the Shaykh's proof is to say thus, but it is not correct because this is exactly the Shaykh's doctrine — that existence is not additional externally but rather mentally; if it were additional externally, impossibilities would follow. And he has admitted this, so how can it be an answer? This agrees with what is in Sharḥ Ḥikmat al-ʿAyn that the dispute is about its being additional in the external, but the commentator said in his glosses: Apparently the dispute is about its being additional in reality, and in relation to the mind is according to the external. And the most excellent of investigators stated this in his Tajrīd where he said: 'So its additionalness in conception. No.'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a complete dialectical argument about the relationship between existence (wujud) and essence (mahiyya) — specifically, the claim that existence is not something added to essence but is either identical to it or a part of it. The passage begins with a proof: if existence were additional to essence, then there would have to be another existence for that additional existence to subsist in, leading to an infinite regress of existences. Since such a regress is impossible, there must be an existence with no intermediary between it and essence — that existence is identical to essence. The proof then points out that the regress of additional existences would require a prior existence for the essence because a non-existent cannot have positive attributes. That prior existence cannot be additional; otherwise the assumption of a final regress would fail; it must be identical to essence. 

The answer from the defender of the additionalness of existence is that the necessity claimed only applies to positive attributes other than existence. Intuitive reason testifies that every positive attribute besides existence requires the prior existence of the subject; but existence itself is the opposite: existence cannot be preceded by another existence, because that would make the thing existent twice, or involve self-precedence, or lead to infinite regress. Thus existence is unique among attributes in not requiring a prior existence. 

Then an objection is raised: this answer is a case of 'takhsis' (specifying a universal rational judgment with an exception), which is not allowed in certain rational judgments. The commentary enters into a detailed discussion about the nature of takhsis: it is permissible when a conflicting evidence is present, but not when the evidence simply does not apply. The commentator (al-Jurjani) explains that the specification here is based on the fact that existence is different from other attributes in its necessity. He refutes a counter-objection by distinguishing between external subsistence and mental subsistence: the necessity of a prior existence only applies when the attribute subsists externally; but existence subsists mentally, not externally, so no regress follows. The commentary then addresses several further objections: that this mental distinction implies that external things need the mind to exist; that it leads to infinite regress in mental existences; and that it admits the Shaykh's (al-Razi's) doctrine rather than answering it. Each objection is refuted: the mental attribution is abstractive, not real; the mental regress is in considerations, not actual; and the Shaykh's real view is about external additionalness, which this answer denies. Finally, the passage corrects a false statement of the 'correct' answer and clarifies the real point of contention: existence is not additional externally, but only conceptually. The entire discussion proceeds through proof, answer, objection, and multiple layers of defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that existence is just like any other attribute and must be preceded by a subject.
Correction: Existence is unique: it is the first actuality and cannot be preceded by another existence.

Checkpoint
What is the objection raised against the defender's answer?
A) It contradicts intuition.
B) It is a case of unjustified specification (takhsis).
C) It leads to an infinite regress.
D) It denies the reality of existence.

Key Takeaway
The defender claims existence is unique and cannot be preceded; the objector calls this arbitrary specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector accused the defender of making an arbitrary exception. When in your life have you dismissed a valid distinction as arbitrary because it challenged your assumptions? Are you willing to accept that some things are truly unique and not bound by the same rules you apply to everything else?
?
This lesson argues that existence cannot be preceded by another existence. How does this affect your understanding of the relationship between God's essence and His existence? Do you truly believe that God's existence is incomparable to any other attribute, or do you still subconsciously treat it like any other quality?
?
The defender used rational intuition to claim that existence is unique. Have you ever relied on a similar intuitive certainty about something fundamental, even when others called it arbitrary? How will you strengthen your trust in such intuitions when they align with the truth?

Refining the Answer: Mental Subsistence and Abstractive Description
Refined answer explaining mental subsistence and abstractive description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refined answer that distinguishes external subsistence from mental subsistence, resolving the objections.

Core Idea
Existence subsists in the mind, not externally, so no regress of external existences occurs.

The commentary deepens the discussion by clarifying that the subsistence of existence in essence is mental and abstractive, not external. This distinction answers the objections about infinite regress and the need for the mind to make things exist. The lesson also addresses the compatibility with the Shaykh's doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the refined answer passage
Begin with 'بل الصواب أن يقال' and read through to the end.
This part corrects a misstatement and provides the final position.
2
Understand the key distinction
The correct answer is that existence is not an external attribute; it is mentally abstracted.
3
See how it avoids objections
Since subsistence is mental, no external regress occurs; the mind analyzes the essence.
4
Relate to the Shaykh's doctrine
The refined answer aligns with the Shaykh's view that existence is not additional in the external.

الشيخ أن يقال : كذا وليس بصحيح لأن هذا عين مذهب الشيخ وهو أن الوجود ليس زائداً في الخارج، بل في العقل إذ لو كان زائداً في الخارج لزم المحالات، وقد سلم هذا فكيف يكون جواباً عنه وهذا يوافق ما في شرح
